     3‚Üí# Awesome-Virome
     4‚Üí
     5‚Üí[![Awesome](https://awesome.re/badge.svg)](https://awesome.re)
     6‚Üí[![Data Update Status](https://github.com/shandley/awesome-virome/actions/workflows/simplified-update-workflow.yml/badge.svg)](https://github.com/shandley/awesome-virome/actions/workflows/simplified-update-workflow.yml)

    10‚Üí<br clear="left"/>
    11‚Üí
    12‚Üí## What is Awesome-Virome?
    13‚Üí
    14‚ÜíA comprehensive, curated database of **300+ software tools** for virome analysis - the study of viral communities in various environments. This repository helps researchers navigate the complex landscape of tools for analyzing phages, viruses, and their interactions with hosts.
    15‚Üí
    16‚Üí**üéØ Perfect for:**
    17‚Üí- Researchers new to virome analysis seeking guidance
    18‚Üí- Experienced scientists looking for specific tools
    19‚Üí- Developers building viral analysis workflows
    20‚Üí- Students learning computational virology
    21‚Üí
    22‚Üí**üöÄ Key Features:**
    23‚Üí- Curated collection of 300+ tools across 8 major categories
    24‚Üí- Interactive dashboard with visualization and analytics
    25‚Üí- Tool comparison matrix with filtering and export
    26‚Üí- Automated metadata collection from GitHub/GitLab/Bitbucket
    27‚Üí- RESTful API for programmatic access
    28‚Üí- Weekly updates and quality assurance
    29‚Üí
    30‚Üí## Quick Start Guide
    31‚Üí
    32‚Üí**New to virome analysis?** Here are the essential tools to get you started:
    33‚Üí
    34‚Üí| Analysis Step | Recommended Tools | Purpose |
    35‚Üí|---------------|-------------------|---------|
    36‚Üí| **1. Viral identification** | VirSorter2, VIBRANT, geNomad | Find viral sequences in metagenomic data |
    37‚Üí| **2. Quality control** | CheckV | Assess viral genome completeness and quality |
    38‚Üí| **3. Host prediction** | iPHoP, CHERRY | Predict which hosts viruses infect |
    39‚Üí| **4. Genome annotation** | Pharokka, DRAMv | Annotate viral genes and functions |
    40‚Üí| **5. Taxonomy assignment** | vConTACT2, PhaGCN | Classify viruses taxonomically |
    41‚Üí
    42‚Üí**Basic Virome Analysis Workflow:**
    43‚Üí1. Quality control of metagenomic reads
    44‚Üí2. Assembly of contigs (e.g., SPAdes, MEGAHIT)
    45‚Üí3. Identification of viral contigs ‚Üí [Virus and Phage Identification](#virus-and-phage-identification)
    46‚Üí4. Quality assessment ‚Üí [Genome Analysis](#genome-analysis)
    47‚Üí5. Taxonomic classification ‚Üí [Taxonomy](#taxonomy)
    48‚Üí6. Host prediction ‚Üí [Host Prediction](#host-prediction)
    49‚Üí7. Functional annotation ‚Üí [Functional Analysis](#functional-analysis)
    50‚Üí
    51‚Üí**üéØ Quick Access:**
    52‚Üí- [**Browse All Tools by Category**](#virus-and-phage-identification) ‚Üì
    53‚Üí- [**Interactive Dashboard**](https://shandley.github.io/awesome-virome/dashboard.html) - Visualize tool relationships
    54‚Üí- [**Tool Comparison Matrix**](https://shandley.github.io/awesome-virome/comparison.html) - Compare tools side-by-side
    55‚Üí- [**Selection Guide**](https://shandley.github.io/awesome-virome/selection-guide.html) - Get personalized recommendations
    56‚Üí

   144‚Üí## Typical Workflows
   145‚Üí
   146‚Üí### Basic Virome Analysis Workflow:
   147‚Üí1. Quality control of metagenomic reads
   148‚Üí2. Assembly of contigs (e.g., SPAdes, MEGAHIT)
   149‚Üí3. Identification of viral contigs ‚Üí [Virus and Phage Identification](#virus-and-phage-identification)
   150‚Üí4. Quality assessment ‚Üí [Genome Analysis](#genome-analysis)
   151‚Üí5. Taxonomic classification ‚Üí [Taxonomy](#taxonomy)
   152‚Üí6. Host prediction ‚Üí [Host Prediction](#host-prediction)
   153‚Üí7. Functional annotation ‚Üí [Functional Analysis](#functional-analysis)
   154‚Üí
   155‚Üí### Advanced Analysis Options:
   156‚Üí- **Strain reconstruction**: [Viral Strain Reconstruction](#viral-strain-reconstruction)
   157‚Üí- **Host-virus interactions**: [Interaction Analysis](#interaction-analysis)
   158‚Üí- **Evolutionary analysis**: [Evolutionary Analysis](#evolutionary-analysis)
   159‚Üí- **Specialized environments**: [Other Tools](#other-tools)
   160‚Üí
   161‚Üí> **üí° Tip**: New to virome analysis? Start with the [Quick Start Guide](#quick-start-guide) above for essential tool recommendations.

   168‚Üí
   169‚Üí- [Cenote-Taker 3](https://github.com/mtisza1/Cenote-Taker3) [v0.1.0, 2023] - Hallmark gene discovery, gene annotation, flanking host gene removal. [Linux/MacOS] [conda] [v0.1.0, 2023]
   170‚Üí- [Cenote-Taker 2](https://github.com/mtisza1/Cenote-Taker2) [v2.1.5, 2022] - Scans contigs for virus hallmark genes, removes flanking host DNA from prophages, makes annotated genome maps. [conda, pip] [v2.1.5, 2022]
   171‚Üí- [CoCoNet](https://github.com/Puumanamana/CoCoNet) [Updated: 03/2025] - Neural networks for viral contig identification. [pip] [Python]
   172‚Üí- [crassus](https://github.com/dcarrillox/CrassUS) [Updated: 04/2023] - Snakemake workflow for phage discovery. [conda] [Python]
   173‚Üí- [DBSCAN-SWA](https://github.com/HIT-ImmunologyLab/DBSCAN-SWA/) [Updated: 12/2024] - DBSCAN clustering for phage identification. [Python]
   174‚Üí- [Deep6](https://github.com/janfelix/Deep6) [Updated: 03/2024] - Machine learning based virus identification. [Python]
   175‚Üí- [DeepVirFinder](https://github.com/jessieren/DeepVirFinder) [Updated: 03/2025] - Neural network approach for viral contig identification. [Python]
   176‚Üí- [DePhT](https://github.com/chg60/DEPhT) [Updated: 12/2024] - Deep-learning Phage Taxonomy for phage identification. [conda] [Python]

   262‚Üí- [iPHoP](https://bitbucket.org/srouxjgi/iphop/src/main/) [v1.3.3, 2023] - Integrated approach for phage host prediction. Documentation at [https://bitbucket.org/srouxjgi/iphop/src/main/](https://bitbucket.org/srouxjgi/iphop/src/main/) [v1.3.3, 2023]. [bioconda] [Python] [v1.3.3, 2023]
   263‚Üí- [MVP](https://web.archive.org/web/20201204203350/http://mvp.medgenius.info/home) [unavailable] - Microbe-virus database with prediction tools. [web service]
   264‚Üí- [PB-LKS](https://github.com/wanchunnie/PB-LKS) [Updated: 02/2025] - K-mer profiles for phage-bacteria prediction. [Python]
   265‚Üí- [PhageHostLearn](https://github.com/dimiboeckaerts/PhageHostLearn) [Updated: 02/2025] - Machine learning for phage-host prediction. [Python]

   344‚Üí## Databases
   345‚Üí
   346‚Üí- [FDA ARGOS](https://argos.igs.umaryland.edu/) - Curated database of reference genomes of microbial sequences, for diagnostic use. [web service] [Updated 2023]
   347‚Üí- [ICTV Virus Metadata Resource (VMR)](https://ictv.global/vmr) - Curated database of sequences of exemplars for each classified virus species. [Updated 2023]
   348‚Üí- [NCBI RefSeq](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/refseq/) - Curated database of annotated genomic, transcript, and protein sequence records: viruses (ca. 8500 complete viral genomes), prokaryotes, eukaryotes. [Updated 2023]
   349‚Üí- [NCBI GenBank](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/genbank/) - Uncurated database of all publicly available nucleotide sequences, annotated. [Updated 2023]
   350‚Üí- [Reference Viral DataBase (RVDB), nucleic version](https://rvdb.dbi.udel.edu/) - Curated database of virus nucleotide sequences, available as Unclustered (U-) and Clustered (C-) nucleotide sequence files. [Updated 2023]
   351‚Üí- [Reference Viral DataBase (RVDB), protein version](https://rvdb-prot.pasteur.fr/) - Protein version (RVDB-prot and RVDB-prot-HMM) of the curated U-RVDB described above. [Updated 2023]
   352‚Üí- [SIB Viral reference sequences](https://viralzone.expasy.org/6096) - Curated database of annotated viral genomes generated by the Swiss Institute of Bioinformatics (SIB). [Updated 2023]
   353‚Üí- [UniProt Virus proteomes](https://www.uniprot.org/proteomes/) - Curated and annotated database of proteomic virus references (ca. 10,000 virus reference proteomes). [Updated 2023]
   354‚Üí- [VirMet](https://github.com/medvir/VirMet) [Updated: 11/2024] - In-house database download from GenBank of viral references. [Python]
   355‚Üí- [Virosaurus](https://viralzone.expasy.org/8676) - Curated database of virus sequences for clinical metagenomics, clustered (non-redundant). [Updated 2022]
   356‚Üí- [Virus Pathogen Resource (ViPR)](https://www.viprbrc.org/) - Curated database of virus pathogens (ca. 1,000,000 genomes from ca. 7000 species). [web service] [Updated 2023]
   357‚Üí- [Virion](https://github.com/viralemergence/virion) [Updated: 02/2025] - An open database of vertebrate-virus interactions. [R]

   490‚Üí- [ViQuaS](https://web.archive.org/web/20190710131744/https://github.com/HadiNW/ViQuaS) [unavailable] - Viral Quasispecies reconstruction. [Python]

   559‚Üí- **Interactive Network**: Discover relationships between tools, categories, and subcategories

   561‚Üí- **Publication Impact Network**: Explore how tools connect to significant research publications
   562‚Üí- **Tool Timeline**: Visualize the evolution of the virome analysis tool ecosystem
   563‚Üí- **Programming Languages**: Analyze technology trends across the tool collection

   570‚Üí

   572‚Üí- Filter by category, language, maintenance status, and more

   592‚Üí
   593‚Üí## Introduction to Virome Analysis
   594‚Üí
   595‚ÜíVirome analysis involves studying the collection of viruses (including bacteriophages) in a specific environment such as the human gut, soil, or oceans. These analyses typically include:
   596‚Üí
   597‚Üí1. Identifying viral sequences in metagenomic data
   598‚Üí2. Classifying viruses and predicting their hosts
   599‚Üí3. Assembling and annotating viral genomes
   600‚Üí4. Analyzing viral diversity and evolution
   601‚Üí5. Studying virus-host interactions and functional potential
   602‚Üí
   603‚Üí> **Note on Tool Availability**: This list contains tools developed over many years. Some tools may no longer be actively maintained or might have moved to new locations. We mark tools that are no longer available as [unavailable] and provide archive links when possible. If you find a broken link or know of a tool's new location, please submit a PR or issue.
   604‚Üí
   605‚Üí## Contributing
   606‚Üí
   607‚ÜíPlease feel free to [contribute](CONTRIBUTING.md)!
   608‚Üí
   609‚ÜíThis repository welcomes contributions from the community. Here's how you can help:
   610‚Üí
   611‚Üí1. **Add New Tools**: Submit entries for tools not yet included in the list
   612‚Üí2. **Update Information**: Help keep tool descriptions and links up to date
   613‚Üí3. **Report Issues**: Let us know about broken links or outdated information
   614‚Üí4. **Improve Documentation**: Suggest enhancements to the documentation
   615‚Üí5. **Fix Bugs**: Help resolve issues with the website or dashboard
   616‚Üí
   617‚ÜíWe provide standardized issue templates to make contributing easier:
   618‚Üí- **Tool Addition**: Template for suggesting new tools
   619‚Üí- **Tool Update**: Template for updating existing tool information
   620‚Üí- **Bug Report**: Template for reporting issues with the repository
   621‚Üí- **Feature Request**: Template for suggesting new features
   622‚Üí
   623‚ÜíFor more details, see our [contribution guidelines](CONTRIBUTING.md).
   624‚Üí
   625‚Üí## Repository Maintenance
   626‚Üí
   627‚ÜíThis repository uses a streamlined GitHub Actions workflow system to maintain data and deployments:
   628‚Üí
   629‚Üí1. **Automated Updates**: Weekly basic updates and monthly comprehensive metadata updates
   630‚Üí2. **Data Management**: All data is stored in `data.json` and displayed through GitHub Pages
   631‚Üí3. **Contribution Flow**: External contributors can propose changes via Pull Requests
   632‚Üí4. **API Access**: Programmatic access to the database via a [REST API](API.md)
   633‚Üí5. **Automated Changelog**: Monthly release notes documenting tool additions, updates, and removals
   634‚Üí
   635‚ÜíFor technical details, see the [workflow documentation](.github/workflows/README.md) and [view our release notes](https://github.com/shandley/awesome-virome/releases).
   636‚Üí
   637‚Üí## Enhanced Metadata
   638‚Üí
   639‚ÜíThis repository features an enhanced metadata collection system that enriches tool information with details from GitHub, GitLab, and Bitbucket repositories:
   640‚Üí
   641‚Üí- **Repository Statistics**: Star counts, forks, open issues, and watchers
   642‚Üí- **License Information**: License type and details for each tool
   643‚Üí- **Programming Languages**: Primary and secondary languages used
   644‚Üí- **Repository Topics/Tags**: Topic classifications from repository metadata
   645‚Üí- **Release Information**: Latest release version and date
   646‚Üí- **Creation & Update Dates**: When repositories were created and last updated
   647‚Üí
   648‚ÜíThis metadata is updated monthly and integrated into our visualization and search capabilities, making it easier to discover tools based on popularity, language preferences, or specific features.

   651‚Üí
   652‚ÜíThis list was originally started by [Rob Edwards](https://github.com/linsalrob) and his team at [Flinders University](https://edwards.flinders.edu.au) and would not have been possible without their original hard work and dedication.
   653‚Üí
   654‚Üí## API Support
   655‚Üí
   656‚ÜíAwesome-Virome provides a REST API that allows programmatic access to the curated database of virome analysis tools. This enables developers and researchers to build applications, workflows, or custom analyses on top of the dataset.
   657‚Üí
   658‚Üí### API Features
   659‚Üí
   660‚Üí- **Base URL:** `https://shandley.github.io/awesome-virome/api/v1/`
   661‚Üí- **Format:** All endpoints return JSON
   662‚Üí- **Authentication:** No authentication required
   663‚Üí- **CORS-Enabled:** Accessible from browser applications
   664‚Üí
   665‚Üí### Key Endpoints
   666‚Üí
   667‚Üí- **All Tools:** `/api/v1/tools.json` - Complete list of all tools with metadata
   668‚Üí- **Categories:** `/api/v1/categories.json` - List of all tool categories
   669‚Üí- **Search Index:** `/api/v1/search.json` - Lightweight index for client-side filtering
   670‚Üí- **Statistics:** `/api/v1/stats.json` - Aggregate statistics about the tools collection
   671‚Üí- **Category-Specific:** `/api/v1/categories/{category_slug}.json` - Tools filtered by category
   672‚Üí
   673‚Üí### Usage Examples
   674‚Üí
   675‚ÜíThe API can be used with standard HTTP requests in any programming language:
   676‚Üí
   677‚Üí```javascript
   678‚Üí// JavaScript example
   679‚Üífetch('https://shandley.github.io/awesome-virome/api/v1/tools.json')
   680‚Üí  .then(response => response.json())
   681‚Üí  .then(data => {
   682‚Üí    console.log(`Found ${data.count} tools`);
   683‚Üí    // Use the data for visualization, filtering, etc.
   684‚Üí  });
   685‚Üí```
   686‚Üí
   687‚ÜíFor complete documentation and additional examples in Python and R, see the [API documentation](API.md).
   688‚Üí

   723‚Üí## Maintenance
   724‚Üí
   725‚Üí### Automated Update Checking
   726‚Üí
   727‚ÜíThis repository includes a Python script (`update_check.py`) that automatically checks when each GitHub, GitLab, and Bitbucket repository was last updated. To use it:
   728‚Üí
   729‚Üí1. Clone this repository
   730‚Üí2. Install required packages: `pip install requests`
   731‚Üí3. Set your GitHub API token (optional, but recommended to avoid rate limits):
   732‚Üí   ```
   733‚Üí   export GITHUB_TOKEN=your_github_token
   734‚Üí   ```
   735‚Üí4. Run the script:
   736‚Üí   ```
   737‚Üí   python update_check.py
   738‚Üí   ```
   739‚Üí
   740‚ÜíThe script will:
   741‚Üí- Check all repository URLs in the README
   742‚Üí- Fetch the last update time for each repository
   743‚Üí- Update the README with [Updated: MM/YYYY] tags
   744‚Üí- Mark unavailable repositories with [unavailable]
   745‚Üí- Generate an `unavailable_repos.md` file listing all repositories that returned 404 errors
   746‚Üí- Save all results to `repo_updates.json` for future reference
   747‚Üí
   748‚ÜíFor better results, run this script periodically to keep the list current.
   749‚Üí

I've reviewed the Awesome-Virome project! Here's a comprehensive overview:

Project Overview

Awesome-Virome is a curated database of 300+ bioinformatics tools for virome analysis (studying viral communities in various environments). It serves as a comprehensive resource for researchers, students, and developers working with phages, viruses, and viral metagenomics.

Key Features

Core Components

  1. Curated Tool Database - 300+ tools across 8 major categories:
  2. Virus & Phage Identification
  3. Host Prediction
  4. Genome Analysis (annotation, assembly, completeness)
  5. Taxonomy
  6. Functional Analysis
  7. Databases & Sequence Resources
  8. CRISPR Analysis

  9. Specialized tools (structural analysis, metatranscriptomics, etc.)

  10. Interactive Web Interface

  11. Dashboard with network visualizations (dashboard.html)
  12. Tool comparison matrix (comparison.html)
  13. Selection guide for personalized recommendations (selection-guide.html)

  14. Citation analytics and publication impact visualizations

  15. RESTful API - Programmatic access at api/v1/ with endpoints for:

  16. All tools, categories, search index, statistics

  17. Category-specific queries

  18. Automated Infrastructure

  19. GitHub Actions workflows for weekly/monthly updates
  20. Automated metadata collection from GitHub/GitLab/Bitbucket
  21. Citation system and metrics tracking
  22. Quality assurance and health checks

Recent Accomplishments

Citation System V2 Phase 1 (Recently Deployed)

  • Complete rebuild using free GitHub API
  • Enhances 164 GitHub tools with comprehensive metrics
  • Integrated into automated workflows
  • Running live in production

README Reorganization

  • Improved user experience with 38% faster time-to-value
  • Added Quick Start Guide
  • Better tool categorization and navigation

Technical Architecture

Data Storage

  • data.json - Main tool database (164 GitHub tools actively tracked)
  • metadata/ - Individual tool metadata files (156+ JSON files)
  • metrics_history/ - Historical tracking of tool metrics

Automation & Scripts

Located in scripts/: - GitHub metrics enhancement - github_metrics_enhancer.py, github_metrics_workflow.py - Citation data collection - Multiple citation-related scripts - Data quality - Validators, quality metrics, schema validation - API generation - generate_api.py - Cache management - Cache warming, monitoring, maintenance

Workflows (.github/workflows/)

  • simplified-update-workflow.yml - Core update workflow (weekly/monthly)
  • Site health checks
  • Cache maintenance
  • Badge generation

Current Status

  • Phase: Citation System V2 Phase 1 Complete & Deployed
  • Branch: main (all work integrated)
  • Next Phases Planned:
  • Phase 2: Basic publication data (DOI resolution)
  • Phase 3: Citation counts (Semantic Scholar, CrossRef, PubMed)
  • Phase 4: Visualizations and analytics

Development Philosophy

  • Incremental, safe development (each phase = separate PR)
  • Free APIs only (no premium dependencies)
  • GitHub Actions for automation (reliable, transparent)
  • Production-ready error handling

The project is well-organized, actively maintained, and provides significant value to the viral bioinformatics research community through its comprehensive tool database and interactive features.

# Claude Code Project Context - Awesome-Virome

## üéØ Project Overview
**Awesome-Virome** is a curated database of 300+ bioinformatics tools for virome analysis, featuring:
- Interactive web dashboard and tool comparison matrix
- RESTful API for programmatic access
- Automated metadata collection and updates via GitHub Actions
- Citation tracking and metrics visualization

## üèóÔ∏è System Architecture

### Core Data Infrastructure
- **`data.json`** - Main tool database (300+ tools, 164 GitHub repos actively tracked)
- **`metadata/`** - Individual tool metadata files (150+ JSON files)
- **`metrics_history/`** - Historical metrics tracking

### Automated Workflows
- **Weekly/Monthly Updates**: `simplified-update-workflow.yml`
  - Basic repo metadata updates (weekly)
  - Comprehensive metrics enhancement (monthly)
  - GitHub API-based metrics collection (stars, forks, languages, topics)
- **Site Health**: Automated validation and health checks
- **Cache Maintenance**: Cache warming and management

### Citation & Metrics System
- **Phase 1** (Deployed): GitHub metrics enhancement
  - `scripts/github_metrics_enhancer.py` - Core logic
  - `scripts/github_metrics_workflow.py` - Production version
- **Future Phases**: DOI resolution, citation counts (Semantic Scholar, CrossRef, PubMed)

## üìÅ Key File Locations

### Core Data & Config
- `data.json` - Main tool database
- `README.md` - User-facing documentation with Quick Start Guide
- `requirements.txt` - Python dependencies
- `.github/workflows/` - GitHub Actions automation

### Scripts (`scripts/`)
- **Metadata**: `github_metrics_*.py`, `enhance_metadata.py`, `enhanced_repo_metadata.py`
- **Data Quality**: `validate_*.py`, `data_quality_metrics.py`
- **API**: `generate_api.py`
- **Citations**: `citation_*.py`, `pubmed_citations.py`, `academic_impact.py`
- **Utilities**: `update_check.py`, `cache_*.py`

### Web Assets
- `dashboard.html`, `comparison.html`, `selection-guide.html` - Interactive tools
- `js/` - Visualization libraries
- `api/v1/` - Generated REST API endpoints

## üõ†Ô∏è Development Practices

### Git Workflow
- Work on `main` branch or feature branches
- Small, incremental PRs (avoid massive merges)
- Each major feature = separate PR

### API Usage
- **Free APIs only** - No premium dependencies
- GitHub API: 5000 req/hr with token
- Future: Semantic Scholar, CrossRef, PubMed (all free)

### Automation Philosophy
- GitHub Actions over local execution
- Production-ready error handling
- Graceful degradation on failures

## üöÄ Quick Start Commands

```bash
# Check project status
git status
git log --oneline -10

# View recent workflow runs
gh run list --limit=5

# Test GitHub API connectivity
python scripts/test_github_api.py

# Validate data quality
python scripts/validate_tool_schema.py

# Generate API endpoints
python scripts/generate_api.py
```

## üìä Project Statistics
- **300+** curated tools across 8 categories
- **164** GitHub repositories actively tracked
- **150+** metadata files with comprehensive tool info
- **Weekly** automated updates
- **Monthly** comprehensive metrics enhancement

     3‚ÜíScript to fix DOIs with trailing parentheses in the data.json file
     4‚Üí"""
     5‚Üí
     6‚Üíimport json
     7‚Üíimport sys
     8‚Üífrom pathlib import Path
     9‚Üí
    10‚Üídef fix_dois(data_file="data.json"):
    11‚Üí    """Fix DOIs with trailing parentheses in data.json"""
    12‚Üí    # Load the data
    13‚Üí    with open(data_file, 'r') as f:
    14‚Üí        data = json.load(f)
    15‚Üí    
    16‚Üí    # Track changes
    17‚Üí    changes_made = 0
    18‚Üí    
    19‚Üí    # Fix DOIs
    20‚Üí    for node in data.get("nodes", []):
    21‚Üí        if "doi" in node and node["doi"] and node["doi"].endswith(")"):
    22‚Üí            old_doi = node["doi"]
    23‚Üí            # Remove trailing parenthesis
    24‚Üí            node["doi"] = node["doi"].rstrip(")")
    25‚Üí            print(f"Fixed DOI for {node['name']}: {old_doi} -> {node['doi']}")
    26‚Üí            changes_made += 1
    27‚Üí    
    28‚Üí    # Save the updated data
    29‚Üí    if changes_made > 0:
    30‚Üí        with open(data_file, 'w') as f:
    31‚Üí            json.dump(data, f, indent=2)
    32‚Üí        print(f"Fixed {changes_made} DOIs in {data_file}")
    33‚Üí    else:
    34‚Üí        print("No DOIs needed fixing")

"""

import re
import sys

def remove_duplicate_tags(readme_path):
    """Remove duplicate consecutive [Updated: MM/YYYY] tags from the README file."""
    # Read the README file

     1‚Üí# Citation Data Collection and Management
     2‚Üí
     3‚ÜíThis document provides an overview of how citation data is collected, validated, and managed in the awesome-virome repository.
     4‚Üí
     5‚Üí## Overview
     6‚Üí
     7‚ÜíThe citation system collects real citation data from published papers about virome analysis tools. This data is used to:
     8‚Üí
     9‚Üí1. Provide accurate citation metrics for each tool
    10‚Üí2. Show tool impact in the citation dashboard
    11‚Üí3. Support analysis of the virome tool ecosystem
    12‚Üí
    13‚Üí## Key Principles
    14‚Üí
    15‚Üí- **Real data only**: All citation data is collected from real sources (PubMed, CrossRef, etc.) with no synthetic data generation
    16‚Üí- **Single source of truth**: Each task (data collection, DOI fixing, etc.) has one authoritative source
    17‚Üí- **Maintainable workflows**: Clear separation of responsibilities between workflows
    18‚Üí
    19‚Üí## Authoritative Components
    20‚Üí
    21‚Üí### Scripts
    22‚Üí
    23‚Üí1. **comprehensive_citation_data.py** - The authoritative script for generating `impact_data.json`
    24‚Üí   - Collects data from multiple sources: academic_impact, bioinformatics, and citation reports
    25‚Üí   - Uses only real citation data with no synthetic data generation
    26‚Üí   - Consolidates all available citation information
    27‚Üí
    28‚Üí2. **auto_fix_dois.py** - The authoritative script for DOI format fixing
    29‚Üí   - Used by the `fix-dois.yml` workflow
    30‚Üí   - Automatically fixes common DOI format issues

# Enhanced Citation Management System

This directory contains a comprehensive citation management system for the awesome-virome project. The system is designed to reliably collect, validate, and analyze citation data for bioinformatics tools from multiple authoritative sources.

## Directory Structure

- **api/**: API clients for external citation sources (CrossRef, iCite, Scopus, Web of Science)
  - **sources/**: Implementation of specific citation source clients
- **schemas/**: JSON schemas for validating data structures
- **utils/**: Utility functions for data processing
- **collectors/**: Core components that collect citation data
- **validators/**: Components that validate DOIs and other citation data
- **reports/**: Report generation tools
- **tests/**: Unit and integration tests
- **examples/**: Example scripts for using the citation system
- **archived/**: Legacy citation scripts (for reference only)

## Citation Sources

The system supports multiple citation sources in a prioritized manner:

#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Get Real Citation Data for Awesome-Virome Tools

This script performs a direct query to fetch real citation data for all tools 
in the Awesome-Virome repository that have DOIs. It uses:
1. CrossRef API to get citation counts for DOIs
2. Existing academic impact metadata for supplementary information
3. Existing citation reports for trends and other citation metrics

/Users/scotthandley/Code/awesome-virome/awesome-virome/archive/README.md


# Archive Directory

This directory contains deprecated code, one-time scripts, and legacy systems that are no longer actively used but preserved for reference.

## Contents

### `legacy_scripts/`
One-time fix scripts that have already been run and are no longer needed:
- `fix_doi.py` - Fixed DOIs with trailing parentheses
- `fix_duplicate_tags.py` - Removed duplicate [Updated: MM/YYYY] tags
- `update_alphafold_citations.py` - One-time citation data update
- `fix_cache_json.py` - Cache JSON format fix
- `fix_citation_counts.py` - Citation count fix
- `migrate_cache.py` - One-time cache migration
- `generate_test_cache.py` - Test cache generator
- `phase1_demo.py` - Phase 1 demonstration script

### `old_citation_system/`
Legacy citation management system (Citation System V1) that used premium APIs:
- Complete package with API clients for Scopus, Web of Science, iCite
- Replaced by Citation System V2 Phase 1 (github_metrics_workflow.py)
- Used free GitHub API instead of premium citation APIs
- Archived: November 2025

**Note**: This entire package was replaced by the simpler, more sustainable approach using only free APIs.

### `test_files/`
Debug and test HTML files no longer in active use:
- `debug_urls.html` - URL debugging interface
- `test_publication_impact.html` - Publication impact test visualization
- `test-network.html` - Network visualization test
- `direct_render.html` - Direct rendering test

### `deprecated_docs/`
Documentation for deprecated systems and approaches.

## Why Archive Instead of Delete?

These files are archived rather than deleted to:
1. Preserve institutional knowledge
2. Provide reference for similar future problems
3. Allow recovery if needed
4. Document the evolution of the project

## Restoration

If you need to restore any archived files:
```bash
# Copy file back to original location
cp archive/legacy_scripts/filename.py scripts/

# Or move if permanent restoration
mv archive/test_files/filename.html .
```

---
*Archive created: November 29, 2025*
*Last cleanup: Phase 1 - Safe deletions and legacy code archival*

    39‚Üídef get_year_from_date(date_str: Optional[str]) -> Optional[int]:
    40‚Üí    """Extract year from ISO date string."""
    41‚Üí    if not date_str:
    42‚Üí        return None
    43‚Üí    
    44‚Üí    try:
    45‚Üí        date_obj = datetime.fromisoformat(date_str.replace('Z', '+00:00'))
    46‚Üí        return date_obj.year
    47‚Üí    except ValueError:
    48‚Üí        return None

#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Script to fetch and store enhanced metadata for repositories in the Awesome-Virome list.
This script collects detailed metadata such as:
- License information
- Programming languages
- Repository topics/tags
- Latest release information
- Dependencies (where available)
- Issue count
- Repository creation date

The metadata is stored in structured JSON files in the metadata/ directory.

This script also supports smart cache invalidation, which ensures that when repository
information is updated, all related cached API responses are automatically invalidated.

Additionally, this module provides functions for extracting tool-specific metadata for
integration with the incremental metadata update process.
"""

import os
import re
import sys
import json
import time
import logging
import requests
from pathlib import Path
from datetime import datetime

# Disabled Workflows

This directory contains GitHub Actions workflows that have been disabled because they reference deprecated code or missing scripts.

## Disabled Workflows

### `update-citation-counts.yml`
**Reason**: References missing script `update_citation_counts.py` and archived script `fix_citation_counts.py`
**Disabled**: November 29, 2025
**Note**: Workflow itself notes it's "NOT Authoritative for impact_data.json" - functionality consolidated into `simplified-update-workflow.yml`

### `scopus-test.yml` & `wos-test.yml`
**Reason**: Test workflows for premium APIs (Scopus, Web of Science) that were part of the deprecated Citation System V1
**Disabled**: November 29, 2025
**Note**: Project moved to free APIs only (GitHub API, CrossRef, etc.) in Citation System V2

### `test-citation-system.yml`
**Reason**: Tests the archived `scripts/citation_system/` package (Citation System V1 with premium APIs)
**Disabled**: November 29, 2025
**Note**: Tests Scopus, WOS, and iCite integration - replaced by simpler Phase 1 approach

## Re-enabling Workflows

To re-enable a workflow:

1. **Fix the underlying issues** - Create missing scripts or restore archived code
2. **Move the file back**: `mv .github/workflows/disabled/workflow-name.yml .github/workflows/`
3. **Test locally** if possible before re-enabling
4. **Update documentation** to reflect the change

## Active Workflows

The main active workflows are:
- `simplified-update-workflow.yml` - Core update workflow (weekly/monthly)
- `github_metrics_workflow.py` - Citation System V2 Phase 1 (GitHub metrics)
- `cache-maintenance.yml` - Cache system maintenance
- `simplified-pages-deploy.yml` - GitHub Pages deployment

For a complete list of active workflows, see `.github/workflows/README.md`

# Disabled Workflows

This directory contains workflows that have been disabled or replaced by more streamlined, authoritative workflows.

## Why Workflows Were Disabled

As part of the citation workflow refactoring and repository cleanup:

1. Consolidated responsibilities into clear authoritative workflows
2. Removed synthetic data generation
3. Eliminated redundant functionality
4. Archived deprecated Citation System V1 (premium APIs)
5. Removed references to missing/archived scripts

## Recently Disabled (November 2025 Cleanup)

### `update-citation-counts.yml`
**Reason**: References missing script `update_citation_counts.py` and archived script `fix_citation_counts.py`
**Note**: Workflow itself notes it's "NOT Authoritative for impact_data.json" - functionality consolidated

### `scopus-test.yml` & `wos-test.yml`

     1‚Üí# Smart Caching System for awesome-virome
     2‚Üí
     3‚ÜíThis document describes the smart caching system implemented for the awesome-virome repository's metadata collection tools.
     4‚Üí
     5‚Üí## Overview
     6‚Üí
     7‚ÜíThe smart caching system provides:
     8‚Üí
     9‚Üí1. **Dependency Tracking**: Tracks which cached data is associated with which repositories
    10‚Üí2. **Selective Invalidation**: When a repository is updated, all its cached data is automatically invalidated
    11‚Üí3. **Improved Performance**: Reduces API calls to external services like GitHub, Semantic Scholar, etc.
    12‚Üí4. **Reduced Rate Limiting**: Helps avoid hitting API rate limits by efficiently using cached data
    13‚Üí5. **Performance Metrics**: Tracks cache hits, misses, and efficiency metrics
    14‚Üí6. **Rate Limit Awareness**: Dynamically adjusts behavior based on remaining API quota
    15‚Üí
    16‚Üí## Key Components
    17‚Üí
    18‚Üí### `CacheManager` Class
    19‚Üí
    20‚ÜíThe core of the smart caching system is the `CacheManager` class in `scripts/apis/citations_api.py`. This class:
    21‚Üí
    22‚Üí- Manages cache storage and retrieval
    23‚Üí- Maintains dependency maps between repositories and cached data
    24‚Üí- Provides methods for invalidating caches based on repository updates
    25‚Üí- Validates cache freshness using configurable expiration policies
    26‚Üí- Tracks performance metrics like hits, misses, and invalidations
    27‚Üí- Calculates cache efficiency statistics
    28‚Üí
    29‚Üí### `RateLimiter` Class
    30‚Üí
    31‚ÜíThe enhanced rate limiter in `scripts/apis/citations_api.py` provides:
    32‚Üí
    33‚Üí- Basic rate limiting to space out API requests
    34‚Üí- Dynamic adjustment based on API rate limit headers
    35‚Üí- Intelligent backoff when approaching rate limits
    36‚Üí- Automatic retry logic for rate limit errors
    37‚Üí- Header parsing for various API rate limit formats
    38‚Üí
    39‚Üí### Integration Points
    40‚Üí
    41‚ÜíThe caching system is integrated at several key points:
    42‚Üí
    43‚Üí1. **Repository Metadata Updates**: In `enhance_metadata.py`, when repository metadata is updated, associated caches are automatically invalidated
    44‚Üí2. **API Clients**: All API clients (GitHub, Semantic Scholar, etc.) use the cache manager for data storage and retrieval
    45‚Üí3. **Academic Impact Collection**: The academic impact collector uses the cache manager to efficiently store and retrieve citation data
    46‚Üí
    47‚Üí### Utilities
    48‚Üí
    49‚ÜíA utility script (`clear_cache.py`) is provided for manual cache management:
    50‚Üí
    51‚Üí- View cache statistics
    52‚Üí- Clear all caches
    53‚Üí- Clear caches for specific repositories
    54‚Üí
    55‚Üí## Usage
    56‚Üí
    57‚Üí### API Methods
    58‚Üí
    59‚ÜíThe cache manager provides these core methods:
    60‚Üí
    61‚Üí```python
    62‚Üí# Store data in cache
    63‚Üícache_manager.set(cache_key, data, repo_url=optional_repo_url)
    64‚Üí
    65‚Üí# Retrieve data from cache
    66‚Üídata = cache_manager.get(cache_key)
    67‚Üí
    68‚Üí# Check if cache is valid
    69‚Üíis_valid = cache_manager.is_valid(cache_key)
    70‚Üí
    71‚Üí# Invalidate all caches related to a repository
    72‚Üícache_manager.invalidate_repo_caches(repo_url)
    73‚Üí
    74‚Üí# Invalidate a specific cache entry
    75‚Üícache_manager.invalidate(cache_key)
    76‚Üí
    77‚Üí# Clear all caches
    78‚Üícache_manager.clear_all()
    79‚Üí```
    80‚Üí
    81‚Üí### Command-line Usage
    82‚Üí
    83‚ÜíCache management via command line:
    84‚Üí
    85‚Üí```bash
    86‚Üí# Show cache statistics and performance metrics
    87‚Üípython scripts/clear_cache.py --stats
    88‚Üí
    89‚Üí# Clear all caches
    90‚Üípython scripts/clear_cache.py --clear-all
    91‚Üí
    92‚Üí# Clear caches for a specific repository
    93‚Üípython scripts/clear_cache.py --clear-repo "https://github.com/username/repo"
    94‚Üí```
    95‚Üí
    96‚ÜíExample statistics output:
    97‚Üí
    98‚Üí```
    99‚Üí===== CACHE STATISTICS =====
   100‚ÜíTotal cache entries: 42
   101‚ÜíDependency mappings: 15
   102‚ÜíTotal size: 2.34 MB
   103‚ÜíRepositories tracked: 10
   104‚Üí
   105‚Üí----- Performance Metrics -----
   106‚ÜíCache hits: 156
   107‚ÜíCache misses: 58
   108‚ÜíTotal requests: 214
   109‚ÜíHit rate: 72.9%
   110‚ÜíCache sets: 98
   111‚ÜíCache invalidations: 12
   112‚ÜíEfficiency: 146.9%
   113‚Üí
   114‚Üí----- Top Repositories by Cache Entries -----
   115‚Üí  5a8d7e2b1c9f: 12 entries
   116‚Üí  3f7b2a6c9d4e: 8 entries
   117‚Üí  ...
   118‚Üí============================
   119‚Üí```
   120‚Üí
   121‚Üí## How Repository Dependency Tracking Works
   122‚Üí
   123‚Üí1. When data is cached, it can be associated with a repository URL
   124‚Üí2. Internally, the cache manager creates a dependency mapping between the repository and the cache key
   125‚Üí3. When a repository is updated, the cache manager looks up all dependent cache entries and invalidates them
   126‚Üí4. Dependencies are stored persistently, so they survive across different script runs
   127‚Üí
   128‚Üí## Performance Considerations
   129‚Üí
   130‚Üí- Metadata about repository dependencies is stored in the `_dependencies` subdirectory
   131‚Üí- Performance metrics are stored in the `_metrics` subdirectory
   132‚Üí- Cached data is hashed and stored in the base cache directory
   133‚Üí- Cache expiration is based on file modification times for efficiency
   134‚Üí- The system minimizes disk I/O by only loading mappings when needed
   135‚Üí
   136‚Üí## Rate Limit Awareness
   137‚Üí
   138‚ÜíThe enhanced rate limiter:
   139‚Üí
   140‚Üí1. Extracts rate limit information from API response headers
   141‚Üí2. Tracks remaining quota and reset times
   142‚Üí3. Dynamically adjusts request spacing when quota is low
   143‚Üí4. Implements smart retry logic for rate-limited requests
   144‚Üí5. Supports different header formats used by various APIs
   145‚Üí
   146‚Üí## Testing
   147‚Üí
   148‚ÜíThe caching system includes comprehensive tests to verify functionality:
   149‚Üí
   150‚Üí- **Unit Tests**: Located in `scripts/tests/test_cache_manager.py`
   151‚Üí- **GitHub Actions**: Workflow in `.github/workflows/test_caching.yml` runs tests in CI
   152‚Üí- **Performance Metrics**: Measured during actual usage to verify effectiveness
   153‚Üí
   154‚ÜíTo run the tests:
   155‚Üí
   156‚Üí```bash
   157‚Üí# Run unit tests
   158‚Üípython -m pytest scripts/tests/test_cache_manager.py -v
   159‚Üí
   160‚Üí# Run with coverage measurement
   161‚Üípython -m pytest scripts/tests/test_cache_manager.py -v --cov=scripts/apis/citations_api
   162‚Üí```
   163‚Üí
   164‚ÜíSee `scripts/tests/README.md` for more details on testing.

Tool reply2025-11-29T21:20:40.209Z
     1‚Üí# Enhanced Cache Management System
     2‚Üí
     3‚ÜíThis document describes the enhanced cache management system for the awesome-virome repository.
     4‚Üí
     5‚Üí## Overview
     6‚Üí
     7‚ÜíThe enhanced cache system provides all the features of the original system plus:
     8‚Üí
     9‚Üí1. **Automatic Expiration**: Automatically removes cache entries older than the specified expiry time
    10‚Üí2. **LRU Eviction**: Maintains a "least recently used" tracking system to intelligently remove stale entries
    11‚Üí3. **Size-Based Limits**: Enforces a maximum cache size with automatic eviction when limits are approached
    12‚Üí4. **Performance Metrics**: Tracks detailed metrics including eviction counts and effectiveness
    13‚Üí5. **Background Maintenance**: Runs cache cleanup in a background thread to maintain performance
    14‚Üí6. **Advanced Monitoring**: Provides comprehensive monitoring tools with visualizations
    15‚Üí
    16‚Üí## Configuration
    17‚Üí
    18‚ÜíThe enhanced cache system is configured with these parameters:
    19‚Üí
    20‚Üí| Parameter | Default | Description |
    21‚Üí|-----------|---------|-------------|
    22‚Üí| `cache_dir` | "metadata/cache" | Base directory for cache storage |
    23‚Üí| `expiry_days` | 30 | Number of days before entries automatically expire |
    24‚Üí| `max_size_mb` | 500 | Maximum cache size in MB |
    25‚Üí| `lru_check_interval` | 3600 | How often to check LRU status (seconds) |
    26‚Üí| `size_limit_percentage` | 0.9 | When to start cleanup (% of max size) |
    27‚Üí
    28‚Üí## How It Works
    29‚Üí
    30‚Üí### Automatic Expiration
    31‚Üí
    32‚ÜíCache entries older than `expiry_days` are automatically removed during maintenance cycles. This ensures the cache doesn't accumulate stale data.
    33‚Üí
    34‚Üí### LRU (Least Recently Used) Tracking
    35‚Üí
    36‚ÜíThe system tracks when each cache entry was last accessed. When cache cleanup is needed, the least recently used entries are removed first. This preserves frequently accessed data while removing entries that haven't been used recently.
    37‚Üí
    38‚Üí### Size-Based Eviction
    39‚Üí
    40‚ÜíWhen the cache size exceeds `max_size_mb * size_limit_percentage`, the system automatically removes enough least recently used entries to bring the size down to 80% of the maximum.
    41‚Üí
    42‚Üí### Background Maintenance
    43‚Üí
    44‚ÜíThe cache system runs a background thread that periodically:
    45‚Üí- Checks for and removes expired entries
    46‚Üí- Performs LRU-based cleanup if needed
    47‚Üí- Ensures the cache stays within size limits
    48‚Üí
    49‚Üí## Directory Structure
    50‚Üí
    51‚Üí```
    52‚Üímetadata/cache/
    53‚Üí  |- *.json                   # Cache data files
    54‚Üí  |- _dependencies/           # Repository dependency mappings
    55‚Üí  |- _metrics/                # Performance metrics
    56‚Üí  |- _lru/                    # LRU tracking data
    57‚Üí  |- _monitoring/             # Monitoring history and graphs
    58‚Üí      |- enhanced/            # Enhanced monitoring data
    59‚Üí          |- graphs/          # Performance visualizations
    60‚Üí```
    61‚Üí
    62‚Üí## Monitoring Tools
    63‚Üí
    64‚Üí### Enhanced Monitor Script
    65‚Üí
    66‚ÜíThe `enhanced_monitor_cache.py` script provides comprehensive monitoring:
    67‚Üí
    68‚Üí```bash
    69‚Üí# Basic monitoring
    70‚Üípython scripts/enhanced_monitor_cache.py
    71‚Üí
    72‚Üí# Continuous monitoring
    73‚Üípython scripts/enhanced_monitor_cache.py --continuous --interval 300
    74‚Üí
    75‚Üí# Generate performance graphs
    76‚Üípython scripts/enhanced_monitor_cache.py --graphs
    77‚Üí
    78‚Üí# Export metrics to CSV
    79‚Üípython scripts/enhanced_monitor_cache.py --export-csv
    80‚Üí```
    81‚Üí
    82‚Üí### Maintenance Script
    83‚Üí
    84‚ÜíThe `cache_maintenance.sh` script handles regular maintenance:
    85‚Üí
    86‚Üí```bash
    87‚Üí# Daily maintenance
    88‚Üí./scripts/cache_maintenance.sh daily
    89‚Üí
    90‚Üí# Weekly comprehensive maintenance
    91‚Üí./scripts/cache_maintenance.sh weekly
    92‚Üí
    93‚Üí# Quick snapshot
    94‚Üí./scripts/cache_maintenance.sh snapshot
    95‚Üí```
    96‚Üí
    97‚Üí## Migrating from the Old System
    98‚Üí
    99‚ÜíThe `migrate_cache.py` script handles migration from the old cache system:
   100‚Üí
   101‚Üí```bash
   102‚Üí# Migrate with default settings
   103‚Üípython scripts/migrate_cache.py
   104‚Üí
   105‚Üí# Migrate with custom max size
   106‚Üípython scripts/migrate_cache.py --max-size 1000
   107‚Üí```
   108‚Üí
   109‚Üí## GitHub Actions Integration
   110‚Üí
   111‚ÜíThe repository includes a GitHub Actions workflow (`cache-maintenance.yml`) that automatically runs cache maintenance:
   112‚Üí
   113‚Üí- Daily maintenance runs every day
   114‚Üí- Weekly comprehensive maintenance runs on Sundays
   115‚Üí- Generates and uploads monitoring graphs
   116‚Üí- Updates a cache status badge
   117‚Üí
   118‚Üí## Performance Impact
   119‚Üí
   120‚ÜíThe enhanced cache system improves overall performance by:
   121‚Üí
   122‚Üí- Reducing the number of API requests through better cache retention
   123‚Üí- Preventing unbounded cache growth
   124‚Üí- Automatically refreshing stale cache entries
   125‚Üí- Optimizing disk usage by removing unused entries
   126‚Üí
   127‚Üí## Troubleshooting
   128‚Üí
   129‚ÜíIf you encounter issues with the cache system:
   130‚Üí
   131‚Üí1. Check the maintenance logs in the `logs/` directory
   132‚Üí2. Run a snapshot monitoring to check cache health:
   133‚Üí   ```bash
   134‚Üí   python scripts/enhanced_monitor_cache.py --summary
   135‚Üí   ```
   136‚Üí3. If needed, manually clear the cache:
   137‚Üí   ```bash
   138‚Üí   python scripts/clear_cache.py --clear-all
   139‚Üí   ```
   140‚Üí4. Restore from a backup if available (backups are created during migration)

     1‚Üí# Cache Monitoring System for awesome-virome
     2‚Üí
     3‚ÜíThis document describes the cache monitoring system implemented for the awesome-virome repository's smart caching infrastructure.
     4‚Üí
     5‚Üí## Overview
     6‚Üí
     7‚ÜíThe cache monitoring system provides:
     8‚Üí
     9‚Üí1. **Real-time Performance Metrics**: Collects and analyzes cache performance in real-time
    10‚Üí2. **Historical Trend Analysis**: Tracks changes in cache metrics over time
    11‚Üí3. **Automatic Health Checks**: Evaluates cache health and identifies potential issues
    12‚Üí4. **Visualization**: Generates graphs of key performance indicators
    13‚Üí5. **Scheduled Monitoring**: Supports automated monitoring via cron
    14‚Üí6. **Reporting**: Exports metrics in various formats (JSON, CSV)
    15‚Üí7. **Alerting**: Detects concerning metrics and can trigger alerts
    16‚Üí
    17‚Üí## Key Components
    18‚Üí
    19‚Üí### `monitor_cache.py` Script
    20‚Üí
    21‚ÜíThe core monitoring tool that provides:
    22‚Üí
    23‚Üí- On-demand cache metrics snapshots
    24‚Üí- Continuous monitoring with configurable intervals
    25‚Üí- Historical metrics tracking and comparison
    26‚Üí- Cache health analysis with recommendations
    27‚Üí- Performance graph generation
    28‚Üí- Metrics export
    29‚Üí
    30‚Üí### `cron_cache_monitor.sh` Script
    31‚Üí
    32‚ÜíA shell script for scheduled monitoring:
    33‚Üí
    34‚Üí- Designed to be run by cron for regular monitoring
    35‚Üí- Supports different monitoring modes (snapshot, hourly, daily, weekly)
    36‚Üí- Includes automatic cleanup of old reports
    37‚Üí- Can trigger alerts when cache health issues are detected
    38‚Üí
    39‚Üí### History and Metrics Storage
    40‚Üí
    41‚Üí- Metrics are stored in `metadata/cache/_monitoring/`
    42‚Üí- Historical metrics enable tracking changes over time
    43‚Üí- Time series data allows for trend analysis
    44‚Üí- Performance graphs visualize key metrics
    45‚Üí
    46‚Üí## Monitoring Metrics
    47‚Üí
    48‚ÜíThe system tracks these key metrics:
    49‚Üí
    50‚Üí- **Hit Rate**: Percentage of cache requests that are served from cache
    51‚Üí- **Miss Rate**: Percentage of requests that require fetching fresh data
    52‚Üí- **Efficiency**: Measure of how effectively the cache is being used
    53‚Üí- **Invalidations**: Number of cache entries that have been invalidated
    54‚Üí- **Cache Size**: Total number of entries in the cache
    55‚Üí- **Growth Rate**: How quickly the cache is growing over time
    56‚Üí- **Repository Dependencies**: How many cache entries depend on each repository
    57‚Üí
    58‚Üí## Usage
    59‚Üí
    60‚Üí### Basic Monitoring
    61‚Üí
    62‚ÜíRun a one-time cache check with detailed report:
    63‚Üí
    64‚Üí```bash
    65‚Üípython scripts/monitor_cache.py
    66‚Üí```
    67‚Üí
    68‚Üí### Continuous Monitoring
    69‚Üí
    70‚ÜíMonitor the cache continuously for a specified duration:
    71‚Üí
    72‚Üí```bash
    73‚Üí# Monitor for 1 hour (3600 seconds) with 60-second intervals
    74‚Üípython scripts/monitor_cache.py --continuous --duration 3600 --interval 60
    75‚Üí```
    76‚Üí
    77‚Üí### Generate Performance Graphs
    78‚Üí
    79‚ÜíCreate visualizations of cache performance:
    80‚Üí
    81‚Üí```bash
    82‚Üípython scripts/monitor_cache.py --graphs
    83‚Üí```
    84‚Üí
    85‚Üí### Export Metrics to CSV
    86‚Üí
    87‚ÜíExport historical metrics to CSV for further analysis:
    88‚Üí
    89‚Üí```bash
    90‚Üípython scripts/monitor_cache.py --export-csv --csv-path /path/to/metrics.csv
    91‚Üí```
    92‚Üí
    93‚Üí### Scheduled Monitoring with Cron
    94‚Üí
    95‚ÜíSet up automated monitoring using the cron script:
    96‚Üí
    97‚Üí```bash

   100‚Üí

   110‚Üí
   111‚ÜíExample crontab entries:
   112‚Üí
   113‚Üí```
   114‚Üí# Run hourly monitoring during work hours
   115‚Üí0 9-17 * * 1-5 /path/to/awesome-virome/scripts/cron_cache_monitor.sh hourly
   116‚Üí
   117‚Üí# Run daily summary at midnight
   118‚Üí0 0 * * * /path/to/awesome-virome/scripts/cron_cache_monitor.sh daily
   119‚Üí
   120‚Üí# Run weekly comprehensive report on Sunday
   121‚Üí0 1 * * 0 /path/to/awesome-virome/scripts/cron_cache_monitor.sh weekly
   122‚Üí```
   123‚Üí
   124‚Üí## Health Analysis
   125‚Üí
   126‚ÜíThe monitoring system analyzes cache health based on multiple factors:
   127‚Üí
   128‚Üí- Hit rate below 30% is considered poor
   129‚Üí- Hit rate between 30-50% is considered fair
   130‚Üí- Hit rate above 50% is considered good
   131‚Üí- Negative cache efficiency is a critical warning
   132‚Üí- High invalidation rates may indicate excessive dependency invalidation
   133‚Üí- Rapidly declining hit rates suggest cache configuration issues
   134‚Üí
   135‚ÜíWhen health issues are detected, the system provides specific recommendations for improving cache performance.
   136‚Üí
   137‚Üí## Visualization and Reporting
   138‚Üí
   139‚ÜíThe monitoring system generates several types of visualizations:
   140‚Üí
   141‚Üí1. **Hit Rate vs Miss Rate**: Shows the balance between cache hits and misses
   142‚Üí2. **Cache Efficiency**: Tracks how efficiently the cache is being utilized
   143‚Üí3. **Invalidations**: Shows cache invalidation patterns over time
   144‚Üí4. **Cache Size**: Tracks growth in the number of cached items
   145‚Üí
   146‚ÜíReports include:
   147‚Üí
   148‚Üí- Current metrics snapshot
   149‚Üí- Change compared to baseline
   150‚Üí- Health assessment
   151‚Üí- Specific warnings for potential issues
   152‚Üí- Actionable recommendations to improve performance
   153‚Üí- Insights on positive aspects of cache performance
   154‚Üí
   155‚Üí## Interpreting Metrics
   156‚Üí
   157‚Üí### Hit Rate
   158‚Üí
   159‚Üí- **Good**: >70% - Cache is working effectively
   160‚Üí- **Fair**: 50-70% - Reasonable performance but room for improvement
   161‚Üí- **Poor**: <50% - Cache may need configuration adjustments
   162‚Üí
   163‚Üí### Efficiency
   164‚Üí
   165‚ÜíCalculated as: `(hits - invalidations) / sets * 100%`
   166‚Üí
   167‚Üí- **Good**: >70% - Cache entries are being reused effectively
   168‚Üí- **Fair**: 30-70% - Moderate reuse with some wasted entries
   169‚Üí- **Poor**: <30% - Many cached entries are being invalidated before reuse
   170‚Üí
   171‚Üí### Invalidation Rate
   172‚Üí
   173‚ÜíHigh invalidation rates (>10/hour) may indicate:
   174‚Üí
   175‚Üí- Over-aggressive repository dependency tracking
   176‚Üí- Too many dependencies between repositories and cache entries
   177‚Üí- Frequent repository updates causing cascade invalidations
   178‚Üí
   179‚Üí## Best Practices
   180‚Üí
   181‚Üí1. **Regular Monitoring**: Run daily monitoring to track performance trends
   182‚Üí2. **Baseline Comparison**: Compare current metrics to historical baselines
   183‚Üí3. **Act on Recommendations**: Implement the recommendations provided by the analyzer
   184‚Üí4. **Adjust Cache Expiration**: Tune expiration times based on hit rate patterns
   185‚Üí5. **Review Dependencies**: Optimize repository dependency tracking if invalidation rates are high
   186‚Üí
   187‚Üí## Troubleshooting
   188‚Üí
   189‚Üí### Low Hit Rate
   190‚Üí
   191‚ÜíIf hit rate is consistently low:
   192‚Üí
   193‚Üí- Check if cache expiration times are too short
   194‚Üí- Ensure repository dependency tracking is correctly configured
   195‚Üí- Verify that API clients are using the cache manager properly
   196‚Üí
   197‚Üí### High Invalidation Rate
   198‚Üí
   199‚ÜíIf invalidation rate is excessive:
   200‚Üí
   201‚Üí- Review repository dependency mapping logic
   202‚Üí- Consider more selective dependency tracking
   203‚Üí- Check for repository update patterns causing cascading invalidations
   204‚Üí
   205‚Üí### Disk Space Concerns
   206‚Üí
   207‚ÜíIf cache size is growing rapidly:
   208‚Üí
   209‚Üí- Implement more aggressive expiration for less important data
   210‚Üí- Consider selective cache clearing for oldest entries
   211‚Üí- Review which API responses are being cached

# Cache System Documentation

Comprehensive documentation for the awesome-virome cache management and monitoring system.

## Table of Contents

- [Overview](#overview)
- [Core Components](#core-components)
- [Configuration](#configuration)
- [Usage](#usage)
- [Monitoring](#monitoring)
- [Maintenance](#maintenance)
- [Troubleshooting](#troubleshooting)
- [Best Practices](#best-practices)

## Overview

The awesome-virome cache system provides intelligent, efficient caching for API responses and metadata with:

### Key Features

1. **Dependency Tracking**: Links cached data to specific repositories for intelligent invalidation
2. **Selective Invalidation**: Automatically invalidates related cache entries when repositories update
3. **Automatic Expiration**: Removes entries older than the configured expiry time
4. **LRU Eviction**: Removes least recently used entries when size limits are approached
5. **Size-Based Limits**: Enforces maximum cache size with automatic cleanup
6. **Performance Metrics**: Tracks hits, misses, efficiency, and more
7. **Rate Limit Awareness**: Dynamically adjusts behavior based on API quotas
8. **Background Maintenance**: Runs cleanup automatically to maintain performance
9. **Comprehensive Monitoring**: Real-time metrics, trend analysis, and visualizations

## Core Components

### CacheManager Class

Located in `scripts/apis/citations_api.py`, provides:
- Cache storage and retrieval
- Dependency mapping between repositories and cached data
- Cache invalidation based on repository updates
- Freshness validation with configurable expiration
- Performance metrics tracking

### RateLimiter Class

Located in `scripts/apis/citations_api.py`, provides:
- Basic rate limiting to space out API requests
- Dynamic adjustment based on API rate limit headers
- Intelligent backoff when approaching limits
- Automatic retry logic for rate-limited requests
- Support for various API header formats

### Monitoring Tools

- **enhanced_monitor_cache.py**: Comprehensive monitoring with real-time metrics, trend analysis, and visualizations
- **cache_maintenance.sh**: Scheduled maintenance script for daily/weekly cleanup
- **clear_cache.py**: Manual cache management and statistics

## Configuration

### Cache Parameters

| Parameter | Default | Description |
|-----------|---------|-------------|
| `cache_dir` | "metadata/cache" | Base directory for cache storage |
| `expiry_days` | 30 | Days before entries automatically expire |
| `max_size_mb` | 500 | Maximum cache size in MB |
| `lru_check_interval` | 3600 | LRU check frequency (seconds) |
| `size_limit_percentage` | 0.9 | Cleanup trigger (% of max size) |

### Directory Structure

```
metadata/cache/
  |- *.json                   # Cache data files
  |- _dependencies/           # Repository dependency mappings
  |- _metrics/                # Performance metrics
  |- _lru/                    # LRU tracking data
  |- _monitoring/             # Monitoring history
      |- enhanced/            # Enhanced monitoring data
          |- graphs/          # Performance visualizations
```

## Usage

### API Methods

```python
# Store data in cache
cache_manager.set(cache_key, data, repo_url=optional_repo_url)

# Retrieve data from cache
data = cache_manager.get(cache_key)

# Check if cache is valid
is_valid = cache_manager.is_valid(cache_key)

# Invalidate all caches related to a repository
cache_manager.invalidate_repo_caches(repo_url)

# Invalidate a specific cache entry
cache_manager.invalidate(cache_key)

# Clear all caches
cache_manager.clear_all()
```

### Command-Line Usage

#### View Statistics

```bash
# Show cache statistics and performance metrics
python scripts/clear_cache.py --stats
```

Example output:
```
===== CACHE STATISTICS =====
Total cache entries: 42
Dependency mappings: 15
Total size: 2.34 MB
Repositories tracked: 10

----- Performance Metrics -----
Cache hits: 156
Cache misses: 58
Total requests: 214
Hit rate: 72.9%
Efficiency: 146.9%
============================
```

#### Clear Cache

```bash
# Clear all caches
python scripts/clear_cache.py --clear-all

# Clear caches for a specific repository
python scripts/clear_cache.py --clear-repo "https://github.com/username/repo"
```

## Monitoring

### Enhanced Monitoring

```bash
# Basic monitoring snapshot
python scripts/enhanced_monitor_cache.py

# Continuous monitoring
python scripts/enhanced_monitor_cache.py --continuous --interval 300

# Generate performance graphs
python scripts/enhanced_monitor_cache.py --graphs

# Export metrics to CSV
python scripts/enhanced_monitor_cache.py --export-csv

# Summary status (used in workflows)
python scripts/enhanced_monitor_cache.py --summary
```

### Scheduled Monitoring

Set up cron for automated monitoring:

```bash
# Hourly during work hours
0 9-17 * * 1-5 /path/to/scripts/cron_cache_monitor.sh hourly

# Daily summary at midnight
0 0 * * * /path/to/scripts/cron_cache_monitor.sh daily

# Weekly comprehensive on Sunday
0 1 * * 0 /path/to/scripts/cron_cache_monitor.sh weekly
```

### Key Metrics

- **Hit Rate**: % of requests served from cache
- **Miss Rate**: % of requests requiring fresh data
- **Efficiency**: `(hits - invalidations) / sets * 100%`
- **Invalidations**: Number of entries invalidated
- **Cache Size**: Total number of entries
- **Growth Rate**: Cache growth velocity

### Health Assessment

| Hit Rate | Status | Recommendation |
|----------|--------|----------------|
| >70% | Good | Cache working effectively |
| 50-70% | Fair | Monitor, room for improvement |
| <50% | Poor | Review configuration |

| Efficiency | Status | Meaning |
|------------|--------|---------|
| >70% | Good | Entries reused effectively |
| 30-70% | Fair | Moderate reuse |
| <30% | Poor | Many wasted entries |

## Maintenance

### Automated Maintenance

GitHub Actions workflow (`cache-maintenance.yml`):
- Daily maintenance every day
- Weekly comprehensive on Sundays
- Generates monitoring graphs
- Updates cache status badge

### Manual Maintenance

```bash
# Daily maintenance
./scripts/cache_maintenance.sh daily

# Weekly comprehensive
./scripts/cache_maintenance.sh weekly

# Quick snapshot
./scripts/cache_maintenance.sh snapshot
```

### Migration

Migrate from older cache systems:

```bash
# Migrate with defaults
python scripts/migrate_cache.py

# Migrate with custom max size
python scripts/migrate_cache.py --max-size 1000
```

Note: Backups are created automatically during migration.

## Troubleshooting

### Low Hit Rate

If hit rate is consistently low (<50%):

1. Check cache expiration times (may be too short)
2. Verify repository dependency tracking configuration
3. Ensure API clients use cache manager properly
4. Review invalidation patterns

### High Invalidation Rate

If invalidations are excessive (>10/hour):

1. Review repository dependency mapping logic
2. Consider more selective dependency tracking
3. Check for cascading invalidations from repo updates
4. Reduce unnecessary dependencies

### Disk Space Issues

If cache is growing too rapidly:

1. Implement more aggressive expiration for low-priority data
2. Use selective cache clearing for oldest entries
3. Review which API responses are being cached
4. Adjust `max_size_mb` and `size_limit_percentage`

### Quick Diagnostics

```bash
# Check cache health
python scripts/enhanced_monitor_cache.py --summary

# View detailed stats
python scripts/clear_cache.py --stats

# Check logs
tail -f logs/cache_monitor_*.log
```

## Best Practices

### Development

1. **Associate with repositories**: Always link cached data to repositories when applicable
2. **Validate before use**: Check `is_valid()` before using cached data
3. **Handle cache misses**: Always have a fallback for cache misses
4. **Use rate limiter**: Integrate rate limiter for all API calls

### Operations

1. **Regular monitoring**: Run daily monitoring to track trends
2. **Baseline comparison**: Compare current metrics to historical baselines
3. **Act on recommendations**: Implement health analysis recommendations
4. **Tune parameters**: Adjust expiration and size limits based on patterns
5. **Review dependencies**: Optimize repository dependency tracking

### Performance

1. **Smart invalidation**: Only invalidate what's truly dependent
2. **Batch operations**: Group cache operations when possible
3. **Monitor efficiency**: Track efficiency metric closely
4. **Prewarm cache**: Use `cache_warming.py` for predictable access patterns

## Advanced Topics

### Dependency Tracking

The system creates mappings between repositories and cache keys:

1. When data is cached with `repo_url`, a dependency is recorded
2. Dependencies persist across script runs
3. When a repository updates, all dependent caches are invalidated
4. Dependencies are stored in `metadata/cache/_dependencies/`

### Rate Limiting Strategy

The enhanced rate limiter:

1. Extracts rate limit info from API response headers
2. Tracks remaining quota and reset times
3. Dynamically adjusts spacing when quota is low
4. Implements smart retry with exponential backoff
5. Supports multiple header formats (GitHub, CrossRef, etc.)

### LRU Eviction

Least Recently Used tracking:

1. Access times are recorded for each cache entry
2. When cleanup is needed, oldest entries are removed first
3. Frequently accessed data is preserved longer
4. LRU data stored in `metadata/cache/_lru/`

## Testing

### Unit Tests

```bash
# Run cache manager tests
python -m pytest scripts/tests/test_cache_manager.py -v

# With coverage
python -m pytest scripts/tests/test_cache_manager.py --cov=scripts/apis/citations_api -v
```

### Integration Tests

GitHub Actions workflow `test_caching.yml` runs automated tests in CI.

---

*For questions or issues, see `.github/workflows/README.md` or check the logs in `logs/` directory.*

**Consolidated Documentation**: This document replaces `CACHING.md`, `CACHE_MANAGEMENT.md`, and `CACHE_MONITORING.md` (archived November 2025).

     1‚Üí# Citation Data Collection and Management
     2‚Üí
     3‚ÜíThis document provides an overview of how citation data is collected, validated, and managed in the awesome-virome repository.
     4‚Üí
     5‚Üí## Overview
     6‚Üí
     7‚ÜíThe citation system collects real citation data from published papers about virome analysis tools. This data is used to:
     8‚Üí
     9‚Üí1. Provide accurate citation metrics for each tool
    10‚Üí2. Show tool impact in the citation dashboard
    11‚Üí3. Support analysis of the virome tool ecosystem
    12‚Üí
    13‚Üí## Key Principles
    14‚Üí
    15‚Üí- **Real data only**: All citation data is collected from real sources (PubMed, CrossRef, etc.) with no synthetic data generation
    16‚Üí- **Single source of truth**: Each task (data collection, DOI fixing, etc.) has one authoritative source
    17‚Üí- **Maintainable workflows**: Clear separation of responsibilities between workflows
    18‚Üí
    19‚Üí## Authoritative Components
    20‚Üí
    21‚Üí### Scripts
    22‚Üí
    23‚Üí1. **comprehensive_citation_data.py** - The authoritative script for generating `impact_data.json`
    24‚Üí   - Collects data from multiple sources: academic_impact, bioinformatics, and citation reports
    25‚Üí   - Uses only real citation data with no synthetic data generation
    26‚Üí   - Consolidates all available citation information
    27‚Üí
    28‚Üí2. **auto_fix_dois.py** - The authoritative script for DOI format fixing
    29‚Üí   - Used by the `fix-dois.yml` workflow
    30‚Üí   - Automatically fixes common DOI format issues
    31‚Üí
    32‚Üí### Workflows
    33‚Üí
    34‚Üí1. **Citation Data Collection and Impact Data Generation** (pubmed-citations.yml)
    35‚Üí   - Collects citation data from PubMed and other sources
    36‚Üí   - Generates citation reports
    37‚Üí   - Creates the authoritative `impact_data.json` file using comprehensive_citation_data.py
    38‚Üí
    39‚Üí2. **DOI Format Fixing** (fix-dois.yml)
    40‚Üí   - Runs the authoritative DOI fixing script auto_fix_dois.py
    41‚Üí   - Fixes common DOI formatting issues across all metadata files
    42‚Üí
    43‚Üí3. **Citation Data Validation** (citation-validation-direct.yml)
    44‚Üí   - Validates DOI consistency and data quality
    45‚Üí   - Creates validation reports
    46‚Üí   - Does NOT modify DOIs (this is handled by the DOI Format Fixing workflow)
    47‚Üí
